# Research Dossier — Ciena Corporation

## Organization Snapshot

- **Legal Name**: Ciena Corporation
- **Headquarters**: Hanover, Maryland
- **Founded**: 1992
- **Industry**: Technology / Networking Equipment
- **Revenue**: $5.9B
- **Employees**: 9K+
- **Ownership**: Public (NYSE: CIEN)
- **Geographic Footprint**: Global — North America, EMEA, India (Gurugram), Asia-Pacific. Rejoined S&P 500 Feb 2026.
- **ICP Score**: 85
- **Tier**: Tier 2

## Financial Health & Growth Stage

Revenue: FY2024 ~$4.02B → FY2025 $4.77B (+19%) → FY2026E $5.9-6.3B (+24-32%). Q1 FY2026 $1.43B (+33% YoY). Adj. EPS $1.35 (+111%). Gross margins ~44.7%. Record backlog $5-7B. Consensus Moderate Buy (8 buy, 6 hold). JP Morgan $380; BofA $355. Key pressures: Customer concentration (3 customers = 67% revenue), supply constraints, Blue Planet deteriorating, CEO succession overhang. Tailwinds: AI buildout, WaveLogic 6 leadership, hyperscaler wins.

## Leadership Team Profiles

### Priority Targets for Outreach

**Gary B. Smith** — President & CEO
- Tenure: CEO since May 2001 (25 years)
- Background: UK-born. NSTAC member 2011-2023 (Obama appointee). Telecom career (CASE, Cray, Intelsat).
- Why target: 25-year CEO navigating most significant pivot in Ciena's history. NSTAC service creates direct alignment with McChrystal's national security DNA.

**Marc D. Graff** — SVP & CFO
- Tenure: Joined Aug 2025
- Background: 28 years at Intel (CFO/COO Datacenter & AI Group). CFO at Altera (Intel spin-out).
- Why target: Outsider CFO with AI/data center expertise. Fresh eyes + mandate to scale for $6B+ run rate.

### Full C-Suite & Key Leaders

| Name | Title | Tenure | Background | Notes |
|------|-------|--------|------------|-------|
| Gary B. Smith | President & CEO | CEO since May 2001 (25 years) | UK-born. NSTAC member 2011-2023 (Obama appointee). Telecom career (CASE, Cray, Intelsat). | — |
| Marc D. Graff | SVP & CFO | Joined Aug 2025 | 28 years at Intel (CFO/COO Datacenter & AI Group). CFO at Altera (Intel spin-out). | — |
| David M. Rothenstein | SVP & Chief Strategy Officer | At Ciena since 2001; CSO since Jan 2023 | Former GC (2008-2023). JD George Washington. Lawyer-turned-strategist. | — |
| Sheela Kosaraju | SVP, General Counsel & Interim Chief People Officer | At Ciena since 2010 | JD Wake Forest; BS Mech. Eng. Carnegie Mellon. Dual-hatting as interim CPO. | — |
| Lawton W. Fitt | Independent Board Chair | Appointed Dec 2024 | Former Goldman Sachs partner. Board of Carlyle Group and Progressive Corp. | — |

## Organizational Culture & Structure Signals

**Structure**: Historically hierarchical engineering culture. Recent management flattening — removing layers.

Glassdoor 4.0/5.0 (2,226 reviews); 78% recommend. Positives: ethical culture, strong onboarding, flat team structures. Negatives: 'products company with services culture' identity confusion; manager training gaps; geographic disconnection; 'challenge to figure out who owns what'; reports of mass resignation in certain teams. No permanent CHRO during significant transformation — GC serving as interim CPO.

## Recent News & Trigger Events

- [2026-03-04] — **Q1 FY2026 record revenue $1.43B (+33% YoY); raised guidance to $5.9-6.3B** — Hypergrowth strains organization — scaling 25-33% annually when culture/alignment typically break down.
- [2025-10-01] — **Strategic pivot: exited residential broadband/PON, doubled down on AI infrastructure** — Reorientation requires new capabilities, talent reallocation, cultural buy-in.
- [2025-08-01] — **CFO transition: Moylan retired after 16 years; Graff (ex-Intel) joined** — C-suite turnover + outsider CFO = window for organizational reassessment.
- [2025-09-01] — **5% workforce reduction (~420 people); management flattening** — Restructuring without permanent CHRO is high-risk. Layoffs + growth = whiplash.
- [2024-12-01] — **Lawton Fitt appointed first independent Board Chair** — Governance maturation — board preparing for post-Smith era.
- [2025-06-01] — **Acquired Nubis Communications ($270M) for 'inside the data center' strategy** — M&A integration: absorbing startup into 9,000-person company.
- [2025-12-01] — **Webscale customers surpassed 54% of revenue** — Customer base transformation from diversified telecom to concentrated hyperscaler.

## McChrystal Fit Assessment

**Rating**: Strong
 — Hits nearly every ICP signal. Revenue in sweet spot. CEO's NSTAC service creates natural affinity. No permanent CHRO = structural opening.

**Primary Problem**: 30-year-old company undergoing simultaneous hypergrowth (25-33%) and strategic transformation (telecom to AI) under a 25-year CEO with no succession plan, operating without a permanent CHRO.

**Best Capability Fit**: Team of Teams — pivot from telecom to hyperscaler requires fundamentally different cross-functional alignment. Also: org design (flattening without communication architecture), leadership development (manager gaps, new CFO, CEO succession).

**Likely Objections**

- Revenue up 33% — why do we need help?
- We're a tech company, not military
- Cost sensitivity during heavy investment

**Competitive Landscape**

- McKinsey/BCG — strategy but lack leadership depth
- Korn Ferry — assessment but lack operating model capability
- Deloitte/Accenture — org design but process-heavy

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: Gary, you're growing at 33% while flattening the org and pivoting your customer base. How are you ensuring teams closest to hyperscaler customers have the decision-making authority and information flow they need?
- **Q**: As Ciena shifts from telecom's optical backbone to the 'nervous system of AI,' how is the organizational culture keeping pace? Are the same leadership capabilities that built a $5B company the ones that will build a $10B one?
- **Q**: With a new independent Chair, new CFO, and a 25-year CEO, how is the board thinking about leadership development at the next level?
  *Framing*: Direct at Board Chair Fitt or CFO Graff

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Frame around the growth challenge, not 'you need transformation.' Gary Smith's NSTAC service (2011-2023) is the strongest door-opener — shared national security telecommunications service gives General McChrystal a natural, non-salesy reason to reach out.

# Research Dossier — DraftKings

## Organization Snapshot

- **Legal Name**: DraftKings Inc.
- **Headquarters**: Boston, Massachusetts
- **Founded**: 2011
- **Industry**: Technology / Online Gaming
- **Revenue**: $6.7B
- **Employees**: 5K+
- **Ownership**: Public (NASDAQ: DKNG)
- **Geographic Footprint**: Sportsbook in 30 U.S. states + DC + Ontario + Puerto Rico. Predictions in 38 states. Operations span 13 countries.
- **ICP Score**: 82
- **Tier**: Tier 2

## Financial Health & Growth Stage

Revenue: FY2023 $3.67B → FY2025 $6.06B (+27%) → FY2026E $6.5-6.9B. First profitable year in FY2025. Q4 net income $136.4M. Adj. EBITDA $620M (+242%). Consensus Buy (27 buy, 8 hold). Pressures: G&A grew from 6% to 22% of revenue; state tax escalation; surcharge debacle. Tailwinds: $10B prediction markets TAM; Jackpocket $340M revenue contribution; AI cost reduction.

## Leadership Team Profiles

### Priority Targets for Outreach

**Jason Robins** — Co-Founder, CEO & Chairman
- Tenure: Since founding (2011)
- Background: Duke (Government). Capital One, Vistaprint. 2025 C-Suite Executive of the Year.
- Why target: Ultimate economic buyer navigating company's most complex transformation.

**Jason Park** — Chief Transformation Officer
- Tenure: CFO 2019-2024; CTO May 2024-present
- Background: 11 years PE Operating Partner. Oversaw IPO and growth from $323M to $3.7B as CFO.
- Why target: Entire role is transformation. PE background = speaks value creation language. Directly owns cross-functional integration.

### Full C-Suite & Key Leaders

| Name | Title | Tenure | Background | Notes |
|------|-------|--------|------------|-------|
| Jason Robins | Co-Founder, CEO & Chairman | Since founding (2011) | Duke (Government). Capital One, Vistaprint. 2025 C-Suite Executive of the Year. | — |
| Jason Park | Chief Transformation Officer | CFO 2019-2024; CTO May 2024-present | 11 years PE Operating Partner. Oversaw IPO and growth from $323M to $3.7B as CFO. | — |
| Alan Ellingson | Chief Financial Officer | Joined 2020; CFO since May 2024 | — | — |
| Linda Aiello | Chief People Officer | — | Previously CPO at Qurate, Stitch Fix; senior HR at Salesforce, Uber, LVMH | — |
| Paul Liberman | Co-Founder, President (Global Tech & Product) | Since founding (2011) | — | — |
| Matthew Kalish | Co-Founder, President (North America) | Since founding (2011) | — | — |

## Organizational Culture & Structure Signals

**Structure**: Three co-founders still operationally active. Multiple verticals (Sportsbook, Casino, DFS, Lottery, Predictions) being consolidated into Super App.

Glassdoor 3.9/5 (71% recommend). Career opportunities 3.7 (lowest). Negatives: favoritism, constant reshuffling, 24/7 expectations, marketing analytics 30-40% attrition. Culture described as 'great if you like sports and can hang with the guys.' Silo risk extreme: four verticals forced into single Super App with different regulatory environments.

## Recent News & Trigger Events

- [2026-02-25] — **~5% workforce reduction across 13 countries; second layoffs in three years** — Organizational trauma during transformation. McChrystal's high-stakes transition expertise directly applicable.
- [2026-03-02] — **Investor Day: Super App strategy, $10B prediction markets, $55-80B 2030 TAM** — Four verticals into one platform requires cross-functional alignment and shared consciousness.
- [2026-02-12] — **Q4/FY2025: first profitable year but conservative guidance triggered 13% selloff** — Investor pressure + growth deceleration. Leadership under pressure.
- [2025-12-19] — **DraftKings Predictions launched in 38 states under CFTC regulation** — New regulatory paradigm requires organizational adaptation.
- [2024-05-01] — **Jason Park moved from CFO to newly created CTO role** — Explicit transformation mandate — entry point for McChrystal.
- [2024-08-14] — **Gaming surcharge announced then reversed within days after backlash** — Reveals gaps in stakeholder analysis and decision-making.
- [2024-05-23] — **Completed $750M Jackpocket acquisition** — Post-acquisition integration challenge.

## McChrystal Fit Assessment

**Rating**: Strong
 — Every ICP signal — $6B+ revenue, 5K+ employees, dedicated CTO role, multi-vector disruption, acquisition integration. Squarely in sweet spot.

**Primary Problem**: Simultaneous multi-vector transformation: Super App integration, $750M acquisition, new regulatory domain (CFTC), AI workforce replacement, restructuring — all while shifting from growth-at-all-costs to profitability.

**Best Capability Fit**: Team of Teams — Super App demands shared consciousness across four verticals. Also: org design (CTO needs frameworks), leadership development (scaling founder leadership), culture change (layoffs + Glassdoor signals).

**Likely Objections**

- Already have a CTO — handling internally
- Tech company needs tech consultants
- Margins under pressure
- No military DNA

**Competitive Landscape**

- McKinsey/BCG/Bain — org design
- Accenture — AI implementation
- Korn Ferry — leadership
- McChrystal differentiator: VUCA framework + Team of Teams for structural integration problems

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: You created a Chief Transformation Officer role — what does Jason Park's mandate look like day-to-day, and where is the integration across Sportsbook, Predictions, Casino, and Lottery proving harder than expected?
- **Q**: Your Super App requires four product teams under different regulatory frameworks to share a single customer experience. How are you building shared consciousness across them without slowing any down?
- **Q**: Two rounds of layoffs in three years while asking the org to take on prediction markets, integrate Jackpocket, and launch a Super App. How are you maintaining trust and talent retention?

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Position as 'transformation operating model' conversation. Lead with Team of Teams applied to Super App integration. Avoid military metaphors initially. Jason Park (CTO) = ideal first meeting; Robins (CEO) = the close.

# Research Dossier — Lululemon Athletica

## Organization Snapshot

- **Legal Name**: lululemon athletica inc.
- **Headquarters**: Vancouver, British Columbia, Canada
- **Founded**: 1998
- **Industry**: Retail / Apparel
- **Revenue**: $11.0B
- **Employees**: 39K+
- **Ownership**: Public (NASDAQ: LULU). Notable: Chip Wilson ~4.27%, Elliott Management $1B+ stake
- **Geographic Footprint**: 800+ company-operated stores across ~24 countries. Key markets: US, Canada, China, Australia, UK, South Korea. ~40+ franchised locations in Middle East and Europe.
- **ICP Score**: 81
- **Tier**: Tier 2

## Financial Health & Growth Stage

Revenue: FY2023 $9.6B (+18.6%) → FY2024 $10.6B (+10.1%) → FY2025E $11.0-11.3B (+4-7%). Americas comp sales declined 5% in Q3. International +38%. Gross margin fell from 58.5% to 55.6%; operating margin from 20.5% to 17.0%. Tariff impact ~$320M in FY2026. Consensus Hold (3 buy, 29 hold, 1 sell). Power of Three x2 ($12.5B target) at risk.

## Leadership Team Profiles

### Priority Targets for Outreach

**Meghan Frank** — Interim Co-CEO & CFO
- Tenure: CFO since 2020; joined 2016
- Background: 20+ years retail (Ross Stores, J.Crew). Overseeing product, merchandising, design during interim.
- Why target: Operational anchor during transition. Controls financial levers. Will evaluate advisory through ROI lens.

**Marti Morfitt** — Executive Chair
- Tenure: Board since 2008; Chair since 2022; Executive Chair Dec 2025
- Background: Principal at River Rock Partners. Former CEO of Airborne; President/CEO of CNS Inc.
- Why target: De facto strategic leader during CEO vacuum. Navigating simultaneous Elliott, Wilson, and CEO search pressures. 18-year institutional credibility.

### Full C-Suite & Key Leaders

| Name | Title | Tenure | Background | Notes |
|------|-------|--------|------------|-------|
| Meghan Frank | Interim Co-CEO & CFO | CFO since 2020; joined 2016 | 20+ years retail (Ross Stores, J.Crew). Overseeing product, merchandising, design during interim. | — |
| André Maestrini | Interim Co-CEO & President/CCO | Joined 2021 as EVP International | 14 years at Adidas in senior global roles. Quadrupled international revenues. | — |
| Marti Morfitt | Executive Chair | Board since 2008; Chair since 2022; Executive Chair Dec 2025 | Principal at River Rock Partners. Former CEO of Airborne; President/CEO of CNS Inc. | — |
| Nikki Neuburger | Chief Brand & Product Activation Officer | Joined 2020 | 14 years at Nike (Global Brand VP); Global Head of Marketing at Uber Eats | — |
| Ranju Das | Chief AI & Technology Officer | Joined Sept 2025 | First CAITO in company history. Newly created role. | — |
| Susan Gelinas | Chief People & Culture Officer (SVP) | — | Rose internally from Sr. VP People & Culture | — |

## Organizational Culture & Structure Signals

**Structure**: Co-CEO structure (inherently temporary). Rapid C-suite turnover — 4 departures in 12 months. Regional structure consolidated under one CCO (Maestrini).

Glassdoor 4.0/5.0 (10,300+ reviews). Culture & Values 4.1; Career Opportunities 3.6 (lowest — red flag). Strengths: wellness culture, generous discount, personal development emphasis. Concerns: pressure to 'live and breathe' the brand (some find cult-like); favoritism in promotions; management quality varies by location. 'Operating with more agility' language in restructuring aligns with Team of Teams.

## Recent News & Trigger Events

- [2025-12-11] — **CEO Calvin McDonald announces departure; interim co-CEO structure; Morfitt elevated to Executive Chair** — Leadership vacuum + interim structure creates urgent need for organizational clarity and decision-rights alignment.
- [2025-12-18] — **Elliott Investment Management reveals $1B+ activist stake; pushes Jane Nielsen as CEO candidate** — External pressure on governance. Board must manage activist demands alongside internal transition.
- [2025-12-29] — **Founder Chip Wilson launches proxy fight; nominates 3 directors** — Two-front governance battle with competing visions. Multi-stakeholder environment where shared consciousness delivers.
- [2025-11-01] — **President of Americas Celeste Burgoyne departs; Maestrini named President/CCO** — Fourth C-suite departure in 12 months. Organizational instability at the top.
- [2025-06-01] — **150 corporate layoffs; company cites need to 'operate with more agility'** — Restructuring + 'agility' framing tailor-made for Team of Teams conversation.
- [2025-12-11] — **Q3 FY2025: gross margin -290 bps; Americas comp -5%; tariff impact escalating** — Financial pressure intensifying. Strategic pivot under duress = VUCA environment.
- [2025-09-01] — **Ranju Das appointed first-ever Chief AI & Technology Officer; CIO Julie Averill departs** — Technology transformation underway. New leader integrating into org in flux.

## McChrystal Fit Assessment

**Rating**: Strong
 — Every fit signal — rapid disruption, leadership/culture problems masquerading as strategy, hierarchical structure failing, high-stakes consequences. CEO vacancy + co-CEO structure + two-front governance = urgent, time-limited window.

**Primary Problem**: Cascading leadership crisis (CEO departure, 4 C-suite exits in 12 months, co-CEO interim) + activist investor + founder proxy fight + North America decline + margin erosion + competitive pressure — all at once. Textbook VUCA.

**Best Capability Fit**: Crisis leadership and high-stakes decision-making — board/interim leaders making consequential decisions under extreme pressure. Cross-functional alignment / Team of Teams — co-CEO structure creates decision-rights ambiguity. Leadership development — interim co-CEOs and new CAITO need rapid onboarding.

**Likely Objections**

- Don't want more advisory during CEO search
- Already work with McKinsey/Bain on strategy
- Culture already strong (4.0 Glassdoor)
- Budget sensitivity given margin pressure

**Competitive Landscape**

- McKinsey — likely engaged on strategy/cost optimization [INFERRED]
- Korn Ferry — likely involved in CEO search [INFERRED]
- Bain — Elliott's playbook often involves Bain
- McChrystal differentiator: execution under pressure, not strategy decks

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: How are you maintaining organizational coherence during the CEO transition — particularly with the co-CEO structure and two different external stakeholders pushing competing visions?
- **Q**: With four C-suite departures in twelve months, what's your approach to ensuring the next layer of leadership is ready to carry the organization through — regardless of who the next CEO is?
- **Q**: Lululemon talks about wanting to 'operate with more agility' — what does that actually look like for a 39,000-person organization simultaneously scaling internationally while defending its core?

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Frame around 'leading through contested transitions.' The ask: focused 90-day engagement on leadership alignment and decision-rights architecture during CEO search, with option to expand once permanent leadership is in place.

# Research Dossier — SAIC

## Organization Snapshot

- **Legal Name**: Science Applications International Corporation
- **Headquarters**: Reston, Virginia
- **Founded**: 1969
- **Industry**: Defense / Government IT Services
- **Revenue**: $7.2B
- **Employees**: 24K+
- **Ownership**: Public (NASDAQ: SAIC). Fortune 500.
- **Geographic Footprint**: 40+ U.S. states. Major hubs: Northern Virginia/DC, Huntsville AL, San Diego CA. Limited international (UK MOD, Australia, Canada via subcontracts).
- **ICP Score**: 80
- **Tier**: Tier 1

## Financial Health & Growth Stage

Revenue: FY2025 $7.48B (+3.1% organic) → FY2026 declining ~5.6% YoY. Q3 FY2026 $1.87B. Adj. EBITDA margin 9.9% (expanding despite revenue pressure). FCF >$550M. Backlog $23.8B (1.2x book-to-bill). Consensus: 3 Buy / 5 Hold. Citi target $133. Pressures: DOGE procurement delays, revenue contraction. Tailwinds: $23.8B backlog, SilverEdge acquisition, strong cash generation.

## Leadership Team Profiles

### Priority Targets for Outreach

**Jim Reagan** — CEO
- Tenure: Permanent Feb 2026; interim from Oct 2025
- Background: Nearly 40 years in defense/gov services. Former EVP & CFO at Leidos. SAIC board since Jan 2023.
- Why target: New permanent CEO actively reshaping organization. 'Speed, flexibility, efficiency' language maps directly to Team of Teams. First 100 days = optimal engagement window.

**John K. Tien Jr.** — Board Member
- Tenure: Appointed Dec 2024
- Background: U.S. Army veteran. Former Deputy Secretary of DHS. West Point graduate. Three combat tours in Iraq.
- Why target: Military background creates natural affinity with McChrystal Group. Board-level champion/connector.

### Full C-Suite & Key Leaders

| Name | Title | Tenure | Background | Notes |
|------|-------|--------|------------|-------|
| Jim Reagan | CEO | Permanent Feb 2026; interim from Oct 2025 | Nearly 40 years in defense/gov services. Former EVP & CFO at Leidos. SAIC board since Jan 2023. | — |
| John K. Tien Jr. | Board Member | Appointed Dec 2024 | U.S. Army veteran. Former Deputy Secretary of DHS. West Point graduate. Three combat tours in Iraq. | — |
| Prabu Natarajan | EVP & CFO | Since Jan 2020 | Oversees all financial activities including IR | — |
| Barbara Supplee | EVP, Army Navy Business Group (ANG) | — | Joined 2023; previously VP/GM at GDIT Navy & Marine Corps | — |
| Vinnie DiFronzo | EVP, Air Force, Space & Intelligence Group (AFSI) | — | — | — |
| Deborah Torosian | SVP & Chief Talent Officer | — | Recent hire — signals leadership attention to workforce/culture challenges | — |
| David Urban | Board Member | Appointed Sept 2025 | West Point Class of 1986. Chairman of American Battle Monuments Commission. | — |

## Organizational Culture & Structure Signals

**Structure**: Consolidated from 5 business groups to 3 (ANG, AFSI, Civilian) effective Jan 31, 2026. CTO role merged with Chief Growth Officer. New Chief Talent Officer hired.

Glassdoor 3.9/5.0 (4,822 reviews); 79% recommend. Work-life balance 4.2. Named to Glassdoor 2026 Best Places to Work. Positives: flexible work, growth opportunities. Negatives: management concerns (workload, favoritism), contract-based job insecurity, bureaucratic processes. Gap between 'Best Places to Work' and management complaints suggests inconsistency across business units — hallmark of siloed organizations.

## Recent News & Trigger Events

- [2025-10-23] — **CEO Townes-Whitley departs after 2 years; Reagan named Interim CEO** — C-suite disruption = prime window for leadership advisory. New CEO must establish credibility and unify.
- [2025-11-13] — **5 business groups consolidated to 3; three senior leaders and Chief Innovation Officer depart** — Structural overhaul with significant leadership churn. Team of Teams and cross-functional alignment highest impact.
- [2025-10-15] — **SAIC acquires SilverEdge Government Solutions for $205M** — Post-acquisition integration of agile software company into 24,000-person org.
- [2026-02-17] — **Jim Reagan appointed permanent CEO after 4-month search** — First 100 days as permanent CEO = optimal engagement window.
- [2025-12-04] — **Q3 FY2026: revenue declines 5.6% despite EPS beat** — Revenue pressure from DOGE creates urgency to optimize operations and win rates.
- [2025-09-01] — **DOGE-driven federal procurement delays and personnel turnover** — External disruption forcing adaptation. VUCA environment — McChrystal's core thesis.
- [2025-12-01] — **Major contract wins: $1.4B Pentagon, $928M HOPE 2.0, $242M Navy** — Winning big, but execution across reorganized groups becomes critical.

## McChrystal Fit Assessment

**Rating**: Strong
 — Textbook. Tier 1 industry, $7.5B revenue (sweet spot), 24K+ employees, active CEO transition, reorg, acquisition, DOGE disruption, board loaded with military leaders. Timing exceptional: new permanent CEO Feb 2026.

**Primary Problem**: 24,000-person defense/IT firm navigating simultaneous CEO transition, 5-to-3 group consolidation, post-acquisition integration (SilverEdge), and DOGE-driven market disruption. Needs to move faster, break silos, create shared consciousness across distributed workforce.

**Best Capability Fit**: Team of Teams — directly addresses 5-to-3 consolidation. Leadership development — new CEO, new group leaders, executive departures. Cross-functional alignment — CTO/CGO merger, talent officer hire, innovation office restructuring. Post-acquisition integration — SilverEdge (small, agile) into SAIC (large, matrixed).

**Likely Objections**

- We already have military DNA
- Just reorganized — need to let changes settle
- Budget pressure makes discretionary consulting tough

**Competitive Landscape**

- Booz Allen Hamilton — direct competitor in gov IT, unlikely hired as advisor
- McKinsey/BCG — strategy/org design but lack military credibility
- Korn Ferry — leadership assessment
- McChrystal advantage: military heritage + instant credibility with board (two West Point graduates)

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: You've consolidated five groups into three and stated the goal is 'speed, flexibility, and efficiency.' The hardest part isn't the new org chart — it's getting the Army group and Navy group to actually operate as one team. How are you building shared consciousness across merged groups?
- **Q**: SilverEdge was a 200-person software shop built for agility. SAIC is 24,000 people optimizing for scale. What's your integration philosophy — protecting SilverEdge's DNA or assimilating them?
- **Q**: You both know from military service that the hardest transitions are combining units with different operational tempos. General McChrystal faced the same challenge getting Army, Navy, Air Force, and CIA operating as one force in Iraq. We've codified those lessons.
  *Framing*: Direct at board members Tien or Urban

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Position around 'operating model for the next chapter' — Reagan is building, not repairing. Frame as partner in designing how reorganized SAIC should operate. Lead with Team of Teams as proven model for military-to-corporate transformation. Avoid positioning as response to Townes-Whitley departure.

# Research Dossier — Imperial Oil

## Organization Snapshot

- **Legal Name**: Imperial Oil Limited
- **Headquarters**: Calgary, Alberta, Canada (relocating operations to Edmonton by 2028)
- **Founded**: 1880
- **Industry**: Energy / Oil & Gas
- **Revenue**: $8.5B
- **Employees**: 5K+
- **Ownership**: Public (TSX/NYSE: IMO). ExxonMobil holds 69.6% majority stake.
- **Geographic Footprint**: Upstream: Kearl oil sands, Cold Lake. Downstream: Strathcona Refinery (Edmonton), Sarnia, Nanticoke. Esso retail network across Canada. Corporate functions migrating to Houston and ExxonMobil centers in India, Argentina, Thailand, Brazil.
- **ICP Score**: 78
- **Tier**: Tier 2

## Financial Health & Growth Stage

Revenue: FY2024 ~CA$51.5B. Net income CA$4.79B. Cash from operations CA$5.98B. Record production 438,000 boe/d (highest in 30+ years). Q4 2025: EPS beat by 1.55% but revenue missed by 10.41%. Dividend raised 20% in Q1 2026. Analyst sentiment: Hold. TD Securities: Sell. BMO: downgraded to Market Perform. Restructuring targeting $150M annual savings by 2028.

## Leadership Team Profiles

### Priority Targets for Outreach

**Dan Lyons** — SVP, Finance & Administration
- Tenure: Since May 2018 (~7 years)
- Background: U.S. Army veteran. BA Economics Vassar; MBA Chicago. Joined ExxonMobil 1990. Career across Dallas, Bangkok, Houston, Saudi Arabia, London.
- Why target: U.S. Army veteran — direct connection to McChrystal Group's military network. As finance leader, controls consulting budgets. Deep institutional knowledge. Entry angle: veteran-to-veteran conversation.

**John Whelan** — Chairman, President & CEO
- Tenure: Appointed President Apr 2025; Chairman/CEO May 2025
- Background: From St. John's, Newfoundland. 37-year ExxonMobil career. Previously SVP Upstream at ExxonMobil (13 global business units). Memorial University B.Eng.
- Why target: New CEO executing most significant transformation in Imperial's modern history within first year.

### Full C-Suite & Key Leaders

| Name | Title | Tenure | Background | Notes |
|------|-------|--------|------------|-------|
| Dan Lyons | SVP, Finance & Administration | Since May 2018 (~7 years) | U.S. Army veteran. BA Economics Vassar; MBA Chicago. Joined ExxonMobil 1990. Career across Dallas, Bangkok, Houston, Saudi Arabia, London. | — |
| John Whelan | Chairman, President & CEO | Appointed President Apr 2025; Chairman/CEO May 2025 | From St. John's, Newfoundland. 37-year ExxonMobil career. Previously SVP Upstream at ExxonMobil (13 global business units). Memorial University B.Eng. | — |
| Cheryl Gomez-Smith | SVP, Upstream | Since May 2024 | BS Mech. Eng. Notre Dame; MBA Tulane | — |
| Scott Maloney | VP, Downstream | Since March 2025 | 12+ years in ExxonMobil lubricants, retail fuel. Moved to Calgary 2023. | — |

## Organizational Culture & Structure Signals

**Structure**: Classic integrated oil company with upstream/downstream/corporate divisions. Historically operated with meaningful autonomy from ExxonMobil ('corporate separateness'). The 2025 restructuring collapses that autonomy — centralizing into ExxonMobil's global centers.

Glassdoor 3.3/5.0; Culture & Values 2.9/5 (lowest); only 47% recommend. Indeed 4.0/5. Positives: good people, strong pay, learning opportunities. Negatives: 'slow company,' excessive processes, bureaucracy. [INFERRED] Post-restructuring morale likely significantly worse. Key challenges: identity crisis (becoming ExxonMobil branch vs. autonomous Canadian company), survivor syndrome, knowledge drain (900 departures), two-speed org (operations untouched, corporate gutted), political headwind (Alberta Premier and federal minister publicly criticized).

## Recent News & Trigger Events

- [2025-02-13] — **CEO Brad Corson announces retirement; John Whelan named successor** — New CEO inheriting and executing biggest restructuring. Classic 'new leader, big mandate' moment.
- [2025-09-29] — **20% workforce reduction (~900 jobs), offshoring, Houston migration announced** — Primary trigger. Massive transformation with high execution risk. Team of Teams built for maintaining cohesion during structural change.
- [2025-09-30] — **Alberta Premier and Federal Energy Minister publicly criticize restructuring** — Political backlash adds reputational risk. Must manage external stakeholders while executing internally.
- [2025-10-01] — **Imperial signs deal to sell Quarry Park campus (800,000 sq ft)** — Physical symbol of transformation. Losing HQ = identity-defining moment.
- [2025-12-01] — **Record annual production (438,000 boe/d) despite restructuring** — Operationally strong but restructuring from strength can make alignment harder — 'why fix what's not broken?'
- [2025-12-15] — **2026 guidance: 441-460K boe/d, $2.0-2.2B capex, 20% dividend increase** — Shareholder-returns narrative dominant. Risk: workforce perceives leadership prioritizing shareholders over employees.

## McChrystal Fit Assessment

**Rating**: Strong
 — Textbook opportunity. New CEO, massive workforce reduction, geographic dispersion, identity transformation, political headwinds, high-stakes operating environment. Dan Lyons military connection provides warm entry. Primary risk: ExxonMobil controlling consulting relationship from Houston.

**Primary Problem**: Imperial Oil is eliminating 20% of its workforce, offshoring critical functions, relocating HQ, and fundamentally restructuring its relationship with parent ExxonMobil — under a new CEO, with political opposition, in an industry facing long-term transition pressure. Risk is organizational: maintaining excellence, knowledge, collaboration, and commitment during 2+ years of sustained disruption.

**Best Capability Fit**: Team of Teams — fragmenting into geographically dispersed nodes (Edmonton, Houston, India, Argentina, Thailand, Brazil). Cross-functional alignment — upstream/downstream/corporate silos being physically separated. Leadership development — new CEO, new downstream VP. Culture change — trust destroyed by layoffs/offshoring.

**Likely Objections**

- ExxonMobil manages our consulting relationships
- Internal change management capabilities via ExxonMobil
- Restructuring plan is set — just need to execute
- Budget pressure — entire point is cost reduction

**Competitive Landscape**

- McKinsey — likely involved (ExxonMobil is known McKinsey client) [INFERRED]
- Korn Ferry — strong O&G org consulting practice
- Deloitte — major Calgary energy sector presence
- Internal ExxonMobil resources — biggest competitor

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: You're asking 80% of your people to stay committed while watching colleagues lose their jobs and seeing the company's identity change. How are you maintaining shared purpose across a workforce now spread from Edmonton to Houston to Mumbai?
- **Q**: Dan, you served in the Army — you know what it takes to maintain unit cohesion during reorganization. How is Imperial preserving the knowledge and relationships that keep Kearl and Cold Lake running at record levels while the corporate structure changes?
  *Framing*: Veteran-to-veteran framing with Dan Lyons
- **Q**: The political reaction from Alberta and Ottawa was unusually sharp. How is leadership managing the external narrative while keeping internal execution on track?

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Enter through Dan Lyons (veteran connection, economic buyer) with goal of earning a meeting with Whelan. Frame as 'operational risk mitigation, knowledge transfer velocity, and cross-functional execution speed' — avoid 'culture' language (ExxonMobil culture is engineering-driven and metrics-focused).

Glassdoor 3.2/5.0 (934 reviews) — below semiconductor avg. Positives: safety culture, state-of-art tech, good benefits. Negatives: 'Disconnect between upper management and those who get work done is breathtaking'; lack of ownership and transparency; frequent team structure changes; still rooted in R&D culture vs. high-volume manufacturing mindset; 'huge employee turnover.' CFO explicitly hired as 'Transformation Expert' — company acknowledges it is in transformation mode.

## Recent News & Trigger Events

- [2024-11-01] — **20% workforce reduction (~1,000+ positions); Durham fab closure; Germany expansion abandoned** — Massive organizational trauma. Surviving employees face uncertainty and broken trust.
- [2025-05-01] — **Robert Feurle appointed CEO; Dr. David Emerson joins as first-ever COO (June 2025)** — New leader inheriting demoralized, restructured org. Must build trust and alignment fast.
- [2025-09-29] — **Chapter 11 emergence after 91-day prepackaged restructuring; $4.6B debt eliminated; entire board reconstituted** — Post-bankruptcy identity reset. New ownership, board, mandate. Must redefine culture and operating model.
- [2025-09-01] — **Gregor van Issum appointed CFO — explicitly as 'transformation specialist'** — Company views itself as in active transformation, not just financial recovery.
- [2026-02-04] — **Q2 FY2026 disappoints; guidance below expectations; additional headcount reduction** — Continued pressure means transformation must deliver quickly. No room for slow cultural evolution.
- [2026-03-01] — **Launched industry-first 10kV SiC MOSFET; unveiled 300mm SiC platform for AI data centers** — Strategic ambition exists but executing requires organizational alignment that may not yet exist.

## McChrystal Fit Assessment

**Rating**: Strong
 — High-conviction. Post-bankruptcy rebuilding, near-total leadership turnover, manufacturing consolidation, workforce trauma, VUCA environment. Former Air Force officer as board chairman provides natural entry point.

**Primary Problem**: Multi-dimensional transformation: new leadership team (CEO, CFO, COO, board all replaced in 12 months), post-bankruptcy rebuilding, manufacturing transition (150mm to 200mm, multi-site to mega-fab), cultural shift (R&D to high-volume manufacturing), and strategic pivot (EV-centric to broader markets incl. AI). Workforce has been through layoffs, bankruptcy, CEO firing, and facility closures.

**Best Capability Fit**: Team of Teams — breaking silos between Mohawk Valley manufacturing, Siler City materials, sales, and R&D. Leadership development — entirely new C-suite needs rapid trust and shared consciousness. Crisis leadership — CHIPS Act uncertainty, EV demand softness, competitive pressure = VUCA. Culture change — R&D/academic culture (Cree legacy) to disciplined manufacturing execution.

**Likely Objections**

- Just went through bankruptcy — can't afford premium consulting
- New leadership needs time to settle
- Semiconductor company — military consulting not relevant
- CFO was already a Chief Transformation Officer

**Competitive Landscape**

- McKinsey — dedicated semiconductor practice
- Korn Ferry — leadership assessment / C-suite onboarding
- AlixPartners/Alvarez & Marsal — may already be involved (bankruptcy context)
- McChrystal differentiator: mission-driven Team of Teams model for post-bankruptcy cultural alignment. Chairman Abate's Air Force background = natural entry.

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: You've replaced nearly every senior leader and board member in 12 months while consolidating from multiple facilities to a single mega-fab. How are you building shared consciousness and trust across teams operating in fundamentally new ways?
- **Q**: Glassdoor and your own hiring patterns suggest Wolfspeed is transitioning from R&D culture to high-volume manufacturing culture. In our experience, that's harder than the technology transition itself. How is that going internally?
- **Q**: Your board chairman started his career as an Air Force officer. Our founder built the operating model that transformed Joint Special Operations Command. There may be a shared philosophy about high-performing teams under pressure. Worth exploring?
  *Framing*: Leverage Abate's military background

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Position around 'post-restructuring organizational alignment.' Frame: 'Organizations that emerge from Chapter 11 with new leadership and reduced workforce have a 12-18 month window to establish operating norms that determine success. Most fail not because strategy is wrong but because the organization can't execute fast enough. We help close that gap.'

- **Tier**: Tier 1

## Recent News & Trigger Events

- [2025-03-19] — **Pfizer sells final 7.3% stake for ~$3.3B. Haleon fully independent.** — First time without former parent oversight. Can pursue own organizational identity.
- [2025-08-01] — **Carl Haney appointed Chief R&D Officer (external hire)** — Another senior change adding to team dynamics that need integration.
- [2025-06-01] — **Completed full buyout of China OTC JV (TSKF)** — Integrating previously semi-independent entity into new operating model. Adds complexity.
- [2025-05-01] — **Capital Markets Day: 'Win as One' strategy, GBP 800M productivity target, 1B more consumers by 2030** — Public commitment. CEO has staked reputation on this strategy delivering.
- [2024-11-01] — **Dawn Allen joins as CFO from Mars/Tate & Lyle** — Allen's Mars title 'VP Global Transformation' — hired for transformation credentials alongside financial expertise.

## McChrystal Fit Assessment

**Rating**: Strong
 — Transformation publicly committed and underway. Organizational challenge maps directly to core offering. CEO staked reputation on it. Timing right (mid-2026 deadline). Company large enough for premium advisory.

**Primary Problem**: Transforming a 24,000-person company's entire operating model — from regional geographic structure to category-led six-Operating-Unit model — in ~18 months, while delivering growth acceleration and GBP 175-200M cost savings. Challenge is organizational execution at speed: getting six new unit leaders, new CGO, CTO, CFO, CHRO, and R&D chief to operate cohesively while org chart redraws underneath them.

**Best Capability Fit**: Team of Teams — creating exactly the kind of decentralized multi-unit structure that fails without shared consciousness. Cross-functional alignment — CGO must coordinate Category, Marketing, Strategy, R&D, Supply Chain across six regions. Leadership development — multiple new Executive Committee members who have never worked together.

**Likely Objections**

- Already have a Chief Transformation Officer and detailed plan
- Consumer healthcare, not military/defense
- Focused on cost savings — can't add advisory spend
- Already working with Big 4 / McKinsey [INFERRED]

**Competitive Landscape**

- McKinsey — likely already involved given size and scope
- Korn Ferry — org structure / Executive Committee expansion
- BCG/Bain — consumer goods sector expertise
- Deloitte — technology/process transformation
- McChrystal differentiator: 'Win as One' is literally Team of Teams. No competitor offers the operating model framework for making decentralized structures operate as one.

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: You've committed to making six Operating Units work as one team by mid-2026. What's your plan for building shared consciousness across unit leaders who have historically competed for resources?
- **Q**: Your new CGO role sits at the intersection of Category, Marketing, Strategy, R&D, Supply Chain, and six regional units. How are you ensuring Filippo Lanzi has the connective tissue to lead across all those interfaces without becoming a bottleneck?
- **Q**: With a new CFO, CHRO, CTO, R&D chief, and Chairman all joining in 18 months, your Executive Committee is essentially a startup team inside a GBP 11B company. How are you accelerating team formation?

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Frame as 'lessons from organizations that have successfully decentralized at scale.' Bring case studies. Hook: 'The ones that succeed invest as much in the operating system — how teams connect and share information — as they do in the org chart. The ones that fail assume the new structure creates new behavior. It never does.'

# Research Dossier — Trinseo

**Rating**: Moderate
 — Fit signals exceptional — crisis leadership, cross-cultural silos, massive restructuring, high-stakes environment. Constraint is financial: company heading for Chapter 11 may have limited discretionary spend. Optimal window: pre-filing to prepare leadership, or post-filing when DIP facility enables operational advisory.

**Primary Problem**: Global manufacturer fighting for survival. Must simultaneously restructure balance sheet (likely Chapter 11), close/consolidate plants across borders, retain critical talent despite existential uncertainty, maintain operational continuity, and pivot product portfolio — all while bridging deep US-EMEA cultural divides.

**Best Capability Fit**: Crisis leadership — VUCA in purest form. Team of Teams / cross-functional alignment — US-EMEA silo problem maps directly to shared consciousness model. Culture change — 48% recommendation rate, blocked promotions, eroding trust.

- McKinsey/BCG/Bain — operational turnaround
- Alvarez & Marsal — interim management/restructuring
- Korn Ferry — leadership assessment
- None bring McChrystal's crisis leadership + Team of Teams

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: Frank, you've got 3,100 people across 21 plants on four continents watching bankruptcy headlines. How are you keeping the operators in Tessenderlo and Rho focused on running their lines while lawyers in New York negotiate with creditors?
- **Q**: You merged three business segments last October and you're closing plants in Germany while ramping recycled PMMA in Italy — are your regional leaders actually operating as one team, or still fighting the US-versus-Europe dynamic?
- **Q**: The retention bonuses signal your board wants this leadership team intact. But what about the next two layers down? Who's keeping your plant managers and technical talent from walking?

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Do NOT lead with organizational consulting. Lead with crisis leadership experience. Frame: 'We help leadership teams operate as one when stakes are highest and margin for error is zero.' Position as confidential 45-minute conversation. Offer concrete 4-6 week 'crisis operating rhythm' assessment. Keep initial price modest ($150K-250K) to get in door.

## Organizational Culture & Structure Signals

**Structure**: Shifting from business-line GM model (Square, Cash App, etc. as independent fiefdoms) to functionally oriented structure. Describes itself as 'federation of companies.' AI mandates: every employee required to use generative AI daily with usage in performance evaluations.

Glassdoor ~1,860 reviews; mixed sentiment. Positives: diversity, purpose-driven, innovative culture. Negatives: frequent restructuring (2023-2026 multiple rounds), difficulty completing projects due to constant team changes, heavy AI adoption pressure, high KPIs, leadership development gaps. One employee: 'worst I've felt in four years.' Data scientist publicly quit refusing 90% raise citing survivor's guilt. AI mandates described as 'surveillance-style.' Key challenge: survivor's guilt and trust erosion among remaining 6,000; forced tech adoption without cultural scaffolding; siloed-to-functional reorg.

## Recent News & Trigger Events

- [2026-02-26] — **4,000+ layoffs (40% of workforce); $450-500M charge; AI cited as primary driver** — THE trigger event. Must rebuild organizational identity, trust, and operating model with half the people.
- [2026-02-26] — **Q4 2025: record $1.1B net income, exceeded Rule of 40 for first time** — Financially strong — can afford premium advisory. Contrast between financial strength and organizational upheaval is the pitch.
- [2026-03-01] — **Bloomberg reports 'AI-washing' concerns; employee backlash over mandatory AI use** — If transformation perceived as hollow cost-cutting, faces talent retention crisis and employer brand damage.
- [2026-03-01] — **Naoko Takeda story goes viral — data scientist refuses 90% raise, quits over survivor's guilt** — Symbolic moment crystallizing human cost. The culture crisis McChrystal's empathy + discipline framework addresses.
- [2025-07-23] — **Block added to S&P 500** — Elevated visibility and institutional scrutiny. Execution failures punished by broader investor base.
- [2024-01-01] — **Shift from business-line GM model to functional organization; Prasanna elevated to CTO of all Block** — Structural reorganization already underway. Cross-functional alignment expertise directly applicable.

## McChrystal Fit Assessment

**Rating**: Strong
 — Multiple active trigger events, record profitability (can afford engagement), leadership challenge masquerading as technology problem. Tier 2 (tech company scaling past agility). Revenue above ICP sweet spot but employee count and transformation dynamics make it compelling.

**Primary Problem**: Cutting 40% of workforce, mandating AI fluency, restructuring from siloed business units to functional model — all while maintaining shipping velocity of a company twice its size. Financial results strong but human/organizational execution is where risk lives. Trust eroded, morale at multi-year lows, 'AI-first' narrative faces AI-washing accusations.

**Best Capability Fit**: Team of Teams — Block is literally trying to do more with fewer people by creating smaller, empowered, cross-functional teams. Organizational design — shift from business-line to functional alignment. Culture change / trust-building — rebuilding trust with 6,000 remaining employees who watched half their colleagues leave. Leadership development — Glassdoor explicitly cites maturation gap.

**Likely Objections**

- Tech company needs tech-native advisors, not military consultants
- Jack Dorsey has strong opinions — may view outside advisory as unnecessary
- Just cut 40% of costs; not adding advisory spend
- CTO managing transformation internally with Goose/AI tools

**Competitive Landscape**

- McKinsey/BCG/Bain — strategy/restructuring
- Korn Ferry — org design and leadership
- Accenture — AI transformation consulting
- McChrystal differentiator: Team of Teams directly maps to 'smaller, empowered teams with shared consciousness in VUCA'

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: You've committed to maintaining the output of a 10,000-person company with 6,000. In special operations, smaller teams only outperform larger ones with shared consciousness across every unit. How are you building that connective tissue between Square, Cash App, and the ecosystem?
- **Q**: The Naoko Takeda story and employee backlash signal the 'why' behind this transformation hasn't landed. Organizations that succeed invest as much in rebuilding trust as restructuring headcount. What's your plan for the human side?
- **Q**: You're shifting from business-unit autonomy to functional alignment — one of the hardest transitions, especially under time pressure. What mechanisms maintain cross-functional coordination without recreating bureaucracy?

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Frame around 'The Team of Teams Challenge at Block' — not crisis response, but proactive capability build. 'You've made the hardest decision (cutting 40%). The question is whether the remaining org operates like a smaller version of old Block, or something fundamentally better.' Avoid military metaphors until trust is built. Lead with outcomes. Window is NOW — Q1 2026 restructuring charges landing, first 90 days of new reality.

# Research Dossier — Genuine Parts Company

## Organization Snapshot

- **Legal Name**: Genuine Parts Company
- **Headquarters**: Atlanta, Georgia
- **Founded**: 1928
- **Industry**: Automotive / Industrial Distribution
- **Revenue**: $24.3B
- **Employees**: 58K+
- **Ownership**: Public (NYSE: GPC). 70 consecutive years of increased dividends (Dividend Aristocrat).
- **Geographic Footprint**: 17 countries, 10,800+ locations. U.S., Canada, Mexico, UK, France, Germany, Belgium, Netherlands, Poland, Australia, New Zealand. Global Automotive (NAPA, Repco, Traction) $15.4B. Global Industrial (Motion) $8.9B.
- **ICP Score**: 65
- **Tier**: Tier 1

## Financial Health & Growth Stage

Revenue: FY2025 $24.3B (+3.46%). Auto $15.4B, Industrial $8.9B. FY2025 GAAP net loss $(609M) — driven by $825M non-cash pension settlement charge. Adj. net income $216M. FY2026 guidance: $25.0-25.6B (3-5.5% growth), adj. EPS $7.50-8.00. $225-250M transformation costs in 2026. Consensus Buy (33% Strong Buy, 33% Buy, 33% Hold). Raymond James Strong Buy $145; Evercore $160. Pressures: auto margin compression, tariffs, separation execution risk. Tailwinds: $200M savings achieved, separation expected to unlock value, Dividend Aristocrat confidence.

- Tenure: Since Aug 2024

- Why target: Less than 2 years in role facing the most significant people/culture challenge in GPC's 97-year history — splitting 58K employees into two companies. Newness to GPC may make her more open to external advisory.

## Organizational Culture & Structure Signals

Negatives: 'stuck in the 80s' — slow to change, resistant to modernization; 'upper management out of touch with floor'; many 15-30 year employees resistant to new ways; hierarchical decision-making conflicting with speed needed. Pension termination (2025) = breaking with legacy structures.

## Recent News & Trigger Events

- [2026-02-17] — **Announced separation into two public companies — Global Automotive (NAPA) and Global Industrial (Motion) by Q1 2027** — Once-in-a-century transformation requiring new leadership structures, cultures, operating models for both entities.
- [2025-09-04] — **Elliott Investment Management cooperation agreement; $1B+ activist stake; two new board directors** — Activist pressure accelerates timeline and raises stakes. Leadership under external scrutiny.
- [2024-08-19] — **New CPO (Jenn Hulett) hired from Dollar Tree** — New CPO signals people/culture strategy reset. She has <2 years institutional context — may welcome external advisory.
- [2024-06-01] — **CEO transition: Stengel elevated from President to CEO** — New CEO with transformation mandate. Original title was 'Chief Transformation Officer' — separation is the culmination.
- [2025-06-09] — **North America Auto leadership restructured — Breaux retiring, Masse promoted to new President role** — Leadership transition in largest segment ahead of separation. Building the team for standalone $15B+ company.
- [2026-01-15] — **Board leadership transition — Stengel named Chairman-Elect; Donahue retiring** — Consolidation of authority in Stengel — one leader carrying enormous load through separation.
- [2025-12-01] — **$825M non-cash pension settlement charge; $175M restructuring savings achieved** — Breaking with legacy structures (pension) while executing cost transformation. Simultaneous financial and structural stress.

## McChrystal Fit Assessment

**Rating**: Strong
 — Tier 1 prospect — large industrial undergoing most transformative event in 97-year history. Corporate separation + activist pressure + new leadership + culture challenges + global complexity. Timing ideal: separation announced but execution just beginning (Q1 2027 target).

**Primary Problem**: Separating a 97-year-old, $24B company with 58,000+ employees across 17 countries into two independent public companies — each needing its own leadership, culture, operating model, board, and strategic identity — while executing multi-hundred-million restructuring, navigating activist pressure, and managing volatile tariff environment. This is a leadership, organizational design, and execution-under-pressure problem.

**Best Capability Fit**: Organizational design — designing two standalone operating models from one. Team of Teams — both entities need cross-functional alignment rapidly (automotive spans 10,800+ locations across 17 countries). Leadership development — new teams moving from 'division heads' to 'independent company leaders.' Culture change — 'stuck in the 80s' culture must now move at separation speed.

**Likely Objections**

- Have McKinsey/Bain/BCG advising on separation structure
- Managing costs tightly
- New CPO handling people/culture internally
- Elliott watching spend closely

**Competitive Landscape**

- McKinsey/BCG/Bain — separation economics and strategy
- Korn Ferry — leadership assessment / talent
- AlixPartners — restructuring/cost savings execution
- PwC — Laurie Schupmann (39yr PwC veteran) just nominated to board
- McChrystal differentiator: execution and leadership, not strategy decks. Separating a unified command into two independent operating units while maintaining effectiveness is precisely what JSOC has done.

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: You're standing up two $10B+ public companies from one 97-year-old organization in ~12 months. What's been harder — separating the systems and processes, or separating the identity and culture?
- **Q**: With Elliott on your board and the separation clock ticking, how are you thinking about the leadership bench for two independent companies — especially the layer below C-suite where execution actually happens?
- **Q**: Your Glassdoor reviews describe a culture that's been stable for decades. Stability is a strength — until you need 58,000 people to move in a new direction fast. How are you shifting that culture without losing what made it work for 97 years?

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Frame around separation execution, not strategy. 'The strategy for why you're separating is clear. The hard part is getting 58,000 people across 17 countries to operate as two distinct, high-performing organizations while it's happening. That's a leadership and organizational challenge — the kind of problem we were built to solve.' The military analogy of separating a unified command into two independent operating units is not forced — it is the GPC situation.

# Research Dossier — FleetPride

## Organization Snapshot

- **Legal Name**: FleetPride, Inc.
- **Headquarters**: Las Colinas (Irving), Texas
- **Founded**: 1999
- **Industry**: Industrial Distribution (Heavy-Duty Auto Parts)
- **Revenue**: $3.0B
- **Employees**: 6K+
- **Ownership**: Private, dual PE-backed — American Securities (majority owner, acquired FleetPride) and Platinum Equity (brought TruckPro into the merger). Mark Lovett (American Securities Managing Director) serves as Board Chair.
- **Geographic Footprint**: 450+ locations across the United States and Canada, including 110+ service centers and 6 distribution centers. Concentrated in major trucking corridors and metropolitan areas. Houston, Dallas, and San Antonio presence strengthened by 2025 OTR Fleet Service acquisition.
- **ICP Score**: 79
- **Tier**: Tier 2

## Financial Health & Growth Stage

Estimated ~$3B combined revenue (some sources cite up to $5B post-merger). Moody's noted 'improving operating margin' and expects high-single-digit revenue growth, with EBITDA margin increasing slightly. However, leverage remains elevated at ~6x debt/EBITDA — Moody's previously flagged 'very high leverage, low interest coverage, and weak liquidity attributed to ongoing negative free cash flow.' Debt was restructured in late 2025 with OHA (T. Rowe Price) leading private financing to support the merger. Moody's subsequently withdrew its rating after debt repayment and assigned a stable outlook. The financial picture is stabilizing but still fragile — the integration must deliver cost synergies and revenue growth to service the debt load. PE owners will be focused on a 3–5 year exit timeline, which creates urgency for operational improvement and EBITDA expansion.

## Leadership Team Profiles

### Priority Targets for Outreach

**Tom Greco** — Chief Executive Officer
- Tenure: Since July 2025 (~8 months)
- Background: 40+ years Fortune 500 leadership. CEO of Advance Auto Parts (2016–2023), where he led a multi-year transformation delivering 5 consecutive years of comparable sales growth. Previously CEO of Frito-Lay North America (PepsiCo) for 30+ years. MBA from Richard Ivey School of Business (Western University). Public company board experience.
- Why target: Economic buyer and decision-maker. New CEO leading the most consequential integration in the company's history. His transformation track record at Advance Auto Parts and stated focus on people-and-culture-first integration aligns directly with McChrystal capabilities. He has the mandate, the budget authority, and a proven appetite for organizational change.
- Notes: No military/government background identified. Greco is a proven transformation CEO who values operational discipline and frontline engagement. Publicly stated that FleetPride–TruckPro integration must 'start with people and culture, not spreadsheets.'

## Organizational Culture & Structure Signals

**Structure**: Historically hierarchical, branch-based distribution model. Post-merger, FleetPride operates a dual-track structure: Tom Greco as CEO with Chuck Broadus leading the TruckPro division reporting to him. The 450+ location footprint is inherently decentralized operationally but has traditionally been managed with centralized control from headquarters — a tension that the merger will amplify.

Glassdoor rating of 2.4/5 (based on 316 reviews) with only 21% of employees recommending the company — a significant red flag. Key themes in employee reviews: 'Executive leadership is a nightmare,' 'You feel like a number here, there is no company culture,' 'Nepotism runs rampant,' 'No work-life balance,' and 'They like to micromanage.' Work-life balance rated 2.2/5, culture and values 2.2/5, career opportunities 2.3/5. These scores reflect the pre-Greco, pre-merger FleetPride — but they represent the cultural baseline that must be transformed. The TruckPro workforce brings its own distinct culture, creating a two-cultures-colliding dynamic. Greco's stated focus on people-first integration suggests he recognizes the culture deficit. [INFERRED] The blue-collar, distributed workforce (branch managers, mechanics, parts counter staff) requires a culture change approach that works at the frontline level — not just C-suite workshops. McChrystal's methodology is well-suited to this.

## Recent News & Trigger Events

- [2025-07-23] — **Tom Greco appointed CEO, replacing interim CEO Stefan Crafton** — New CEO with transformation DNA brings a mandate for change and a fresh perspective on organizational design. First 12 months are the prime window for advisory relationships.
  [source](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/fleetpride-appoints-tom-greco-as-chief-executive-officer-302511300.html)
- [2025-10-28] — **FleetPride–TruckPro merger completed, creating largest independent HD aftermarket distributor** — Massive integration challenge: 450+ locations, 6,500+ employees, two distinct cultures, overlapping geographies. Classic McChrystal engagement — building shared consciousness across a newly combined, distributed organization.
  [source](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/fleetpride-and-truckpro-announce-strategic-merger-302596968.html)
- [2025-11-03] — **OHA (T. Rowe Price) leads private debt financing to support the FleetPride–TruckPro merger** — Significant debt restructuring — Moody's noted 'very high leverage' and debt/EBITDA near 6x. Financial pressure means the integration must deliver results quickly; failed integration = existential risk.
  [source](https://www.oakhilladvisors.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/OHA_Fleetpride_Press_Release_20251103-FINAL_.pdf)
- [2025-03-01] — **FleetPride acquires OTR Fleet Service LLC (Houston-based, 3 service centers, 30+ mobile units)** — Continued acquisitive growth even before TruckPro merger — signals integration is a recurring challenge, not a one-time event.
- [2026-02-01] — **CEO Tom Greco delivers keynote at Heavy Duty Aftermarket Dialogue 2026** — Greco is publicly positioning himself as a thought leader in the industry transformation. Public visibility creates outreach opportunities through shared platform appearances or post-event follow-up.
  [source](https://www.mema.org/news/fleetpride-ceo-tom-greco-brings-new-insights-heavy-duty-aftermarket-dialogue-2026)
- [Date unknown] — **Moody's withdraws ratings after FleetPride repays concerning debt; assigns stable outlook with 'improving operating margin'** — Financial stabilization post-restructuring means FleetPride has breathing room to invest in organizational capability — but the high leverage (6x debt/EBITDA) means every dollar spent must show returns. McChrystal engagements can be framed as integration insurance.
  [source](https://www.freightwaves.com/news/truck-parts-supplier-fleetpride-holds-on-to-speculative-debt-ratings)
- [Date unknown] — **Heavy-duty aftermarket industry facing tariff pressures, digital transformation, and electrification shifts in 2025–2026** — Industry-wide disruption compounds internal integration challenges. FleetPride must simultaneously integrate TruckPro AND adapt to structural market changes — the kind of VUCA environment where McChrystal's framework is most compelling.
  [source](https://www.globenewswire.com/news-release/2025/09/19/3153311/28124/en/Heavy-Duty-Truck-Parts-Aftermarket-Industry-to-Grow-by-21-4-Billion-During-2025-2030.html)

## McChrystal Fit Assessment

**Rating**: Strong
 — FleetPride presents a compelling engagement opportunity: new transformation CEO + massive post-merger integration + distributed frontline workforce + high financial leverage creating urgency. Greco's public statements about people-first integration align perfectly with McChrystal's methodology. The primary risk is PE budget sensitivity, but the integration stakes are high enough that a well-framed proposal (integration insurance, not discretionary consulting) should resonate.

**Primary Problem**: Post-merger integration of two large, geographically distributed organizations with distinct cultures, overlapping operations, and a frontline-heavy workforce — all under significant financial leverage and with a new CEO who must establish authority quickly.

**Best Capability Fit**: Team of Teams operating model implementation. FleetPride's challenge is textbook McChrystal: a newly combined organization with 450+ locations needs to build shared consciousness, break down legacy silos (FleetPride vs. TruckPro), and empower distributed frontline leaders to execute autonomously while staying aligned. Greco's stated philosophy that integration 'starts with people and culture' is the exact entry point for McChrystal's approach.

**Likely Objections**

- PE owners (American Securities + Platinum Equity) may resist advisory spend given high leverage (6x debt/EBITDA) — must frame as integration risk mitigation and EBITDA protection, not discretionary consulting
- FleetPride may already have integration consultants from PE firms' preferred vendor lists (McKinsey, Bain, AlixPartners) — McChrystal needs to differentiate on culture/leadership vs. operational/financial integration
- Greco's 40+ years of Fortune 500 experience may make him skeptical of outside advisors — need to position McChrystal as a peer-level partner, not a typical consultancy
- Heavy-duty auto parts distribution may feel 'too blue collar' for McChrystal's brand — but the distributed frontline workforce and high-stakes operating environment (fleet downtime = customer revenue loss) are actually ideal fit factors

**Competitive Landscape**

- McKinsey Organization Practice — PE firms often default to McKinsey for post-merger integration; however, McKinsey's approach is typically top-down and analytical, not culture-first
- Bain & Company — strong PE relationships (both American Securities and Platinum Equity are Bain clients); likely has existing relationship for deal diligence
- AlixPartners — common PE-backed integration advisor, but focused on operational/financial restructuring, not leadership and culture
- Korn Ferry — could compete on leadership assessment and executive coaching; lacks McChrystal's operating model and team-based transformation methodology
- Internal PE operating partners — both American Securities and Platinum Equity have operating teams that may be driving integration priorities

## Conversation Entry Points

- **Q**: You've said publicly that the FleetPride–TruckPro integration has to start with people and culture, not spreadsheets. Eight months in, what's been the hardest part of getting 6,500 people across 450 locations to feel like one team?
  *Framing*: Validate Greco's stated philosophy, then pivot to McChrystal's experience building shared consciousness in large, distributed organizations that were forced to integrate quickly (JSOC parallel).
- **Q**: With dual PE ownership and significant leverage, how are you thinking about the balance between integration speed and getting the culture right — especially when every quarter matters to your board?
  *Framing*: Acknowledge the financial pressure without being presumptuous. Position McChrystal as having helped organizations accelerate integration timelines without sacrificing cultural alignment — integration speed as a competitive advantage, not a tradeoff.
- **Q**: The heavy-duty aftermarket is facing tariff disruptions, electrification shifts, and digital transformation all at once. How is FleetPride building the organizational agility to absorb those external shocks while simultaneously integrating TruckPro?
  *Framing*: Frame the VUCA environment — FleetPride faces both internal complexity (integration) and external disruption (market shifts). McChrystal's Team of Teams model was built for exactly this kind of compound uncertainty.

**Recommended First Meeting Framing**: Position as a peer-level conversation about leading large-scale integration in distributed, frontline-heavy organizations. Lead with the JSOC parallel: General McChrystal faced the same challenge of unifying disparate units with distinct cultures into a single, cohesive force capable of moving faster than the threat environment. Avoid 'consulting pitch' framing — Greco has 40 years of experience and will reject anything that feels generic. Offer a specific, concrete insight about post-merger culture integration (e.g., a 90-day shared consciousness accelerator) rather than a broad capabilities overview. If possible, reference a specific PE-backed integration McChrystal has supported.

# Research Dossier — GXO Logistics

## Organization Snapshot

- **Legal Name**: GXO Logistics, Inc.
- **Headquarters**: Greenwich, Connecticut, United States
- **Founded**: 2021
- **Industry**: Logistics & Supply Chain
- **Revenue**: $13.2B
- **Employees**: 130K+
- **Ownership**: Public (NYSE: GXO). Spun off from XPO Logistics in August 2021. No controlling shareholder; institutional investor base.
- **Geographic Footprint**: Operations in approximately 27 countries across North America, Europe, and Asia-Pacific. 1,200+ warehouse and logistics facilities. Major presence in US, UK (expanded via Wincanton acquisition), Continental Europe, and select APAC markets.
- **ICP Score**: 82
- **Tier**: Tier 2

## Financial Health & Growth Stage

**Revenue**: $13.2B FY2025 (record), up 12.5% YoY from $11.7B in FY2024, driven by Wincanton acquisition and 3.5% organic growth. Q4 2025 revenue of $3.5B (+7.9% YoY).

**Profitability**: Adjusted EBITDA of $881M FY2025 (up from $815M), but GAAP diluted EPS dropped sharply from $1.12 to $0.28 — reflecting integration costs, higher interest expense, and one-time items. Adjusted EPS of $2.52 provides a cleaner picture.

**2026 Guidance**: Organic revenue growth of 4-5%, adjusted EBITDA of $930-970M (8% growth), adjusted EPS of $2.85-$3.15 (20% growth). Company expects $50-70M in annual Wincanton synergies by 2026.

**Analyst Sentiment**: Consensus Strong Buy from 11 analysts, average price target $67.91. Investors are cautiously optimistic on margin expansion and integration execution but watching leverage and leadership transition risk.

**Key Pressures**: Integration execution risk on Wincanton, elevated leverage from acquisitions, EPS decline despite revenue growth, multiple simultaneous leadership transitions. **Key Tailwinds**: Record new business wins ($1B+ for third consecutive year), automation-driven productivity gains, margin expansion trajectory, strong 2026 pipeline ($774M incremental revenue).

## Leadership Team Profiles

### Priority Targets for Outreach

**Patrick Kelleher** — Chief Executive Officer
- Tenure: Since August 2025 (~7 months)
- Background: 33 years in global supply chain. Former CEO North America at DHL Supply Chain (Deutsche Post DHL). Led M&A transactions, robotics deployments (Boston Dynamics Stretch), and major operational transformations at DHL. Metrics-driven leader focused on execution and innovation.
- Why target: Economic buyer. New CEO actively reshaping the organization — replaced CRO, created COO role, hired new Americas president. Clearly driving a mandate to build 'his team' and a new operating rhythm. Open to external advisory that accelerates transformation without adding bureaucracy.
- Notes: First external CEO in GXO's history as independent company. Immediately initiated sweeping management restructuring. Operational background suggests comfort with execution-oriented advisory.

**Bart Beeks** — Chief Operating Officer
- Tenure: Since January 2026 (~2 months)
- Background: Career at CEVA Logistics, rising from intern to COO. Managed operations in 170+ countries, led multiple acquisition integrations, drove operating margin improvements. Based in Eindhoven, Netherlands.
- Why target: Internal champion. His mandate — 'standardize global execution' across a fragmented, recently-acquired operation — is the exact problem McChrystal's Team of Teams operating model solves. New to the organization and building his own playbook.
- Notes: Newly created role focused on standardizing global execution. Charged with improving productivity, efficiency, and customer value across 1,200+ sites. Key integration leader for Wincanton.

| Michael Jacobs | President, Americas & Asia Pacific | Since November 2025 (~4 months) | 30+ years in supply chain operations.
